  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_aecfe1ce-0827-419b-9afa-0c65506046db'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer7995977770142245076">To escape a scheme to marry her off to a dishonorable man, Margaret Macy flees London disguised as a housemaid. If she can remain unwed until her next birthday, she will receive an inheritance, and with it, sweet independence. But she never planned on actually working as a servant. And certainly not in the home of Nathaniel and Lewis Upchurch--both former suitors. <br/><br/>As she f</span>
  <span id="freeText7995977770142245076" style="display:none">To escape a scheme to marry her off to a dishonorable man, Margaret Macy flees London disguised as a housemaid. If she can remain unwed until her next birthday, she will receive an inheritance, and with it, sweet independence. But she never planned on actually working as a servant. And certainly not in the home of Nathaniel and Lewis Upchurch--both former suitors. <br /><br />As she fumbles through the first real work of her life, Margaret struggles to keep her identity secret when suspicions arise and prying eyes visit Fairbourne Hall. Can she avoid a trap meant to force her from hiding?<br /><br />Brimming with romance and danger, <i>The Maid of Fairbourne Hall takes readers inside the fascinating belowstairs world of a 19th-century English manor, where appearances can be deceiving.</i></span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/250855592?book_show_action=true">Dec 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer250855592" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12432691151993420881">First posted on my blog, <a href='http://katie-mccurdy.blogspot.com/2012/01/julie-klassen-is-21st-centurys-jane.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Legacy of a Writer</a>.<br/><br/>Julie Klassen is the 21st century's Jane Austen! I knew she was good after reading The Apothocary’s Daughter, but The Maid of Fairbourne Hall really blew me away. Open this book and Klassen will transports you back to the early 1800s, in England, when upper-class Margaret Macy suddenly finds her life altered to that of a lowly housemaid.<br/><br/>The first character that struck me the strongest and grabbed my attention was wild-mannered and dashingly good lookin</span>
  <span id="freeText12432691151993420881" style="display:none">First posted on my blog, <a href="http://katie-mccurdy.blogspot.com/2012/01/julie-klassen-is-21st-centurys-jane.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Legacy of a Writer</a>.<br /><br />Julie Klassen is the 21st century's Jane Austen! I knew she was good after reading The Apothocary’s Daughter, but The Maid of Fairbourne Hall really blew me away. Open this book and Klassen will transports you back to the early 1800s, in England, when upper-class Margaret Macy suddenly finds her life altered to that of a lowly housemaid.<br /><br />The first character that struck me the strongest and grabbed my attention was wild-mannered and dashingly good looking Nathaniel Upchurch. At his first appearance after years in Barabdos, I was glued to the pages and instantly intrigued about this man. Margaret took a little longer for me to warm up to, but through no fault of the author! She was just a bit too uppity. Once she was brought low and humbled as a housemaid—and learned so many lessons about the people who work so hard behind the scenes—she grew on me.<br /><br />For being a rather thick book, I flew through the pages, easily. And found it very hard to put it down at the end of each chapter. Klassen excels at keeping the reader riveted to the pages, both with her awesome, intricate storyplot and her deep, endearing characters.<br /><br />The things that Margaret had to go through as a housemaid certainly made for some amusing moments. Especially her first time at emptying a chamber pot! Haha, I was laughing out loud—how gross! As to questionable content, there really wasn’t any worth mentioning. A few of the male characters have less than honorable designs toward women, especially the servant girls, but details are never given.<br /><br />If you love the Jane Austen classics, then you have to try one of Julie Klassen’s novels and discover that Austen’s brilliance with regency romances lives on! I was swept away in this lovely tale where the reader gets a behind the scenes look at what life was like for the servants in a 19th century English manor. You won’t be disappointed!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12432691151993420881" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_187321540" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/187321540" />
    <a title="Kelly_Instalove" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5853766-kelly-instalove"><img alt="Kelly_Instalove" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1369788195p2/5853766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/187321540?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly_Instalove" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly_Instalove" href="/user/show/5853766-kelly-instalove">Kelly_Instalove</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5853766-kelly-instalove?shelf=era-historical">era-historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5853766-kelly-instalove?shelf=genre-romance">genre-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5853766-kelly-instalove?shelf=genre-inspirational">genre-inspirational</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5853766-kelly-instalove?shelf=theme-disguise">theme-disguise</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5853766-kelly-instalove?shelf=theme-friends2lovers">theme-friends2lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5853766-kelly-instalove?shelf=hist-eng-stuart-georgian">hist-eng-stuart-georgian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer187321540" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17837027642015357189">I'm not one for the fangirl "OMG YOU HAVE TO READ THIS" stuff, but Julie Klassen’s books have tempted me to engage in some literary peer pressure. "It's not a preachy inspirational, trust me!"<br/><br/>I was drawn to her books by the intriguing titles, beautiful covers and well-written blurbs, and all four of her previous novels exceeded my expectations. I've read them all several times, and I still can’t decide which one to add to my Desert Island Keepers.<br/><br/>I had <i>The Maid of Fairbourne Hall</i> on my "yay comi</span>
  <span id="freeText17837027642015357189" style="display:none">I'm not one for the fangirl "OMG YOU HAVE TO READ THIS" stuff, but Julie Klassen’s books have tempted me to engage in some literary peer pressure. "It's not a preachy inspirational, trust me!"<br /><br />I was drawn to her books by the intriguing titles, beautiful covers and well-written blurbs, and all four of her previous novels exceeded my expectations. I've read them all several times, and I still can’t decide which one to add to my Desert Island Keepers.<br /><br />I had <i>The Maid of Fairbourne Hall</i> on my "yay coming soon!!!" wishlist for months and bought it the day it came out. But then it lingered in Mount TBR for another few months because, oddly enough, I was afraid I wouldn’t like it. I call it "Book Anxiety," which I may write an essay or treatise about sometime.<br /><br />ANYWAY, in addition to the run-of-the-Regency-mill title and vaguely disturbing cover photo, I did a mental "huh?" double-take when I saw the "disguised as a servant" plot. <br /><br />And after reading – well, score one for the Book Anxiety.<br /><br /><b>The plot…</b><br /><br />There’s a big drawback to being an obsessive reader (of any genre, not just romance), in that predictable plots begin to make themselves known earlier and more often. As I was reading <i>The Maid of Fairbourne Hall</i>, I found myself shaking my head and even rolling my eyes a few times. And that's <i>never</i> happened with a Klassen book before.<br /><br />All of Klassen's books feature conflicted heroines hiding – literally or metaphorically – from their families. Unlike the unique and compelling situations of her previous novels, however, this one fell flat. It takes a LOT of creativity to make this particular premise work successfully, and unfortunately Klassen just couldn't pull it off.<br /><br /><b>The main characters…</b><br /><br />Nathaniel was a decent beta hero – not quite swoon-worthy, but likeable enough for me to root for <i>his</i> HEA.<br /><br />Margaret, on the other hand, I found to be almost unlikeable, nearly to the point where I didn’t feel she deserved <i>her</i> HEA. Her transformation from spoiled debutante to socially-conscious servant seemed too easy and superficial. She just can’t compare to other Klassen’s previous smart, brave and compelling heroines.<br /><br /><b>Now let me tell you what I REALLY think…</b><br /><br />For me, the biggest deficit was the lack of dramatic tension. I needed a stronger sense of danger to justify Margaret running away, and a MUCH stronger sense of attraction between Margaret and Nathaniel to feel a sustained emotional connection between them.<br /><br />I had to deduct one star for the eye-rolling Very Convenient Coincidence of Margaret/Nora being hired in her former suitor’s house, AND the random and <i>completely</i> unnecessary <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">["poet/pirate" <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> plot diversion.<br /><br />I also had to knock it another half-star for that creepy cover photo (<i>what</i> is wrong with her eyes???). If I wasn’t already a Klassen fan, that cover would NEVER have drawn me in and convinced me this book was worth spending $10. I hate the model's pose and facial expression, and the there’s a weird sort of Bad Photoshop thing that’s really unusual for Bethany House books.<br /><br />However, I still love Klassen's writing style, especially the sense of history and atmosphere she conveys. I also enjoyed the sub-plot with Helen and Hudson – I think THEIR story would have been much more romantic and inspirational.<br /><br />Now I need to go type up my rave reviews for all her other books so I won’t feel so guilty for not loving this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17837027642015357189" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9096003148789976426">4.5<br/>This was a really fun read for me. If I had to quickly explain what this book reminded me of, I'd say it's sort of like mixing Jane Austen's Persuasion with Charles Dickens's A Christmas Carol. The theme of second chances and discovering how their actions and behavior effected those around them, really stood out to me. <br/><br/>I also enjoyed "seeing" and learning more about what life as a servant, specifically as a housemaid, might have been like. The added side stories that involved ships, a poetry </span>
  <span id="freeText9096003148789976426" style="display:none">4.5<br />This was a really fun read for me. If I had to quickly explain what this book reminded me of, I'd say it's sort of like mixing Jane Austen's Persuasion with Charles Dickens's A Christmas Carol. The theme of second chances and discovering how their actions and behavior effected those around them, really stood out to me. <br /><br />I also enjoyed "seeing" and learning more about what life as a servant, specifically as a housemaid, might have been like. The added side stories that involved ships, a poetry speaking pirate, a secret duel, and sugar plantations in Barbados, made the story feel fresh and exciting. <br />There were a few moments that some may roll their eyes at and find incredible, but for me, I really enjoyed it. I found it very hard to put down. </span>

    <a title="Kate" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51950019-kate"><img alt="Kate" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577731463p2/51950019.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1578348496?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate" href="/user/show/51950019-kate">Kate</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51950019-kate?shelf=christian-books">christian-books</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1578348496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7510467925386838666">This is the first book of Julie Klassen that I have read and it will not be my last. I did not think I could enjoy and get as involved in a book as I did with this one. <br/><br/>I want to say one thing before giving my review of the book. Don’t give up on the book. The book is a slow start and I was myself tempted to put it down and skip it. I am so glad that I did not and continued reading on. The story gets better and better and really does a nice job tying everything up at the end. <br/><br/>The story takes you</span>
  <span id="freeText7510467925386838666" style="display:none">This is the first book of Julie Klassen that I have read and it will not be my last. I did not think I could enjoy and get as involved in a book as I did with this one. <br /><br />I want to say one thing before giving my review of the book. Don’t give up on the book. The book is a slow start and I was myself tempted to put it down and skip it. I am so glad that I did not and continued reading on. The story gets better and better and really does a nice job tying everything up at the end. <br /><br />The story takes you back to England 1815 and introduces the reader to the main character Margaret Macy. Margaret is a somewhat spoiled lady and takes her servants and her comforts for granted at times. This though will all change when Margaret must leave her home and hide from her stepfather. Her stepfather has plans of her marrying his nephew, though Margaret has plans of her own. <br /><br />As the book goes on, Margaret along her journey of running away and becoming a house servant herself soon learns the meaning of hard work, honesty, thinking of others and even love. Margaret always had suitors but never really gave any one of them a thought. Except for Lewis and Nathaniel Upchurch. These two brothers have asked for her hand and she refused them. Now living under the same roof with them playing a servant will her heart learn to care for one of them or both? <br /><br />Excellent read and a real treat getting an in depth look at what being a downstairs servant was really like. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7510467925386838666" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1624978888" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16588581135738242390">I enjoyed this one much more than the last couple of Julie Klassen novels I've read. It may be because the heroine wasn't being punished for being a "fallen woman." Thankfully, this one was much less heavy and preachy, not so full of judgment and condemnation. At the most, some Bible verses and a few quick prayers were all that reminded me that this was a Christian romance, thank God. I do like to read a good romance that focuses more on the emotional aspect of love rather than sex scenes, but a</span>
  <span id="freeText16588581135738242390" style="display:none">I enjoyed this one much more than the last couple of Julie Klassen novels I've read. It may be because the heroine wasn't being punished for being a "fallen woman." Thankfully, this one was much less heavy and preachy, not so full of judgment and condemnation. At the most, some Bible verses and a few quick prayers were all that reminded me that this was a Christian romance, thank God. I do like to read a good romance that focuses more on the emotional aspect of love rather than sex scenes, but also doesn't preach at me. Believe it or not, that's hard to find.<br /><br />Mainly, this was a story of a selfish, proud woman who finds herself in the position of a servant and learns what it's like to be on the other side. The upstairs-downstairs aspect was interesting. I do tend to enjoy how Klassen's romances explore aspects of the time period that you don't often get in a romance, making them closer to the Historical Fiction end of the spectrum. Although some of it might have been a bit far-fetched, that's often true of Regency romances. <br /><br />I was able to sit back and enjoy this one. I'm glad I decided to pick it up. I almost didn't after the bitter taste the last couple books had left me.</span>

<div id="review_933990907" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/933990907" />
    <a title="Maria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19799133-maria"><img alt="Maria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1382981396p2/19799133.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/933990907?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria" href="/user/show/19799133-maria">Maria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/12954935-the-maid-of-fairbourne-hall">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19799133-maria?shelf=regency">regency</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19799133-maria?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19799133-maria?shelf=christian-fiction">christian-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer933990907" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15690105823410815811">After hearing a private conversation between her step father and his nephew, in which they plotted to make her marry the young man in order to steal her inheritance, Margaret Macy decides to flee and wait for her upcoming birthday, when she will get that inheritance and will be able to live on her own. With the help of her former maid, Margaret becomes a housemaid in the home of Nathaniel Upchurch, a man she once rejected because she wanted to win his brother’s love. Will she be safe in Nathanie</span>
  <span id="freeText15690105823410815811" style="display:none">After hearing a private conversation between her step father and his nephew, in which they plotted to make her marry the young man in order to steal her inheritance, Margaret Macy decides to flee and wait for her upcoming birthday, when she will get that inheritance and will be able to live on her own. With the help of her former maid, Margaret becomes a housemaid in the home of Nathaniel Upchurch, a man she once rejected because she wanted to win his brother’s love. Will she be safe in Nathaniel’s home? Will Nathaniel expose her, if he finds out her true identity? After all, her refusal is still painful to him to remember...<br /><br />What are the right ingredients for a great book? In my opinion a book must have an engaging plot, endearing characters, a little bit of mystery and breathtaking moments. I can safely say that you can find all those things in every novel by Julie Klassen! She is so talented that I have no difficulty at imagining the scenes she describes. Not only are they interesting and beautiful, and help readers feel a part of the story, but Ms. Klassen always adds historical details that are very useful to understand better the characters and their actions and behaviour. In “The Maid of Fairbourne Hall”, for instance, she tells us the life of the servants in the early 1800s through Margaret’s experiences, but she is never boring and you never get tired of reading her words. Everything is described so well and in a very engrossing way that you have the impression of actually being in the nineteenth-century England. Or if not, you start dreaming of at least visiting those places!<br /><br />Her characters always learn something that will change their lives forever, in a positive way. In the beginning Margaret is spoiled and indifferent towards her servants’ feelings, while by the end of the book she is definitely another person, because her experience changes her and lets her see those people through different eyes. She learns that servants are as worthy of respect as rich people, and even though she should have understood that before, I liked the journey she made which led her to change her mind. <br /><br />Nathaniel Upchurch is adorable! His behaviour towards Margaret and Nora (Margaret’s alter ego) is commendable. There were several moments where I wanted to yell at him because I thought it was impossible for him not to recognise her, nevertheless he was a perfect gentleman every time they had some chances to speak to each other. I loved their relationship and the way it was depicted. <br /><br />I have yet to read all of Julie Klassen’s stories, so I am not in the desperate phase when one freaks out because they have to wait a lot before getting her new book, but I am already worried because that awful day will arrive very soon! I loved every novel that I have read by Ms. Klassen, and I heartily recommend all of them, especially if you love England and Regency era. If you have never read her books, I think this one may be a great start!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15690105823410815811" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_553097212" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/553097212" />
    <a title="Meredith (Austenesque Reviews)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2073558-meredith-austenesque-reviews"><img alt="Meredith (Austenesque Reviews)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504749496p2/2073558.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/553097212?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meredith (Austenesque Reviews)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meredith (Austenesque Reviews)" href="/user/show/2073558-meredith-austenesque-reviews">Meredith (Austenesque Reviews)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer553097212" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8430006500743202763">Margaret Macy must escape her home to protect her virtue, inheritance, and future! Her step-father has ordered his scoundrel nephew to court, woo, and even compromise (if necessary) his step daughter, Margaret, in order to force marriage between them and obtain control of her inheritance. With no funds readily available and no family nearby, Margaret disguises herself as a maid and leaves her family and home. In just a few months she will be old enough to claim her inheritance and can come out o</span>
  <span id="freeText8430006500743202763" style="display:none">Margaret Macy must escape her home to protect her virtue, inheritance, and future! Her step-father has ordered his scoundrel nephew to court, woo, and even compromise (if necessary) his step daughter, Margaret, in order to force marriage between them and obtain control of her inheritance. With no funds readily available and no family nearby, Margaret disguises herself as a maid and leaves her family and home. In just a few months she will be old enough to claim her inheritance and can come out of hiding. Needing protection and the means to support herself, Margaret looks for work as a maid. By chance she is given a trial job at Fairbourne Hall, an estate that sounds familiar to her. It isn’t until Margaret arrives at Fairbourne Hall that she realizes that a former suitor whose offer of marriage she rejected lives within and is now considered her master.<br /><br />With all the time we spend amongst servants and learning about life downstairs, this story felt like a Regency version of Downton Abbey! Julie Klassen shows readers what a normal day’s work is like for a housemaid, the rules and restrictions they must abide by, the isolated and lonely life they can live. I love how Ms. Klassen always includes relevant content and historical backdrops that educates and informs her readers about life in other professions and time periods. I learn so much when I read her novels – like the practice of maids facing a wall when a member of the family is passing near and how servants were required to mix or create their own cleaning materials and household commodities like furniture polish and cold cream.<br /><br />This is my fifth Julie Klassen novel*, so of course I went in expecting a bit of intrigue, personal growth, a tender romance, and inspiration – I was not disappointed! The intrigue about Margaret and her masquerade as a servant was such a fun adventure to follow, and the mysterious activities of Lewis Upchurch and what he was up to at night definitely kept me guessing. But what riveted me most to this story and kept me saying “one chapter more” to myself repeatedly was Nathaniel Upchurch and whether or not he recognized Margaret! I loved, loved, loved the scenes between Nathaniel and Margaret! Nathaniel is a caring, noble, and very admirable hero, and I greatly enjoyed observing Margaret slowly realize bit by bit all his wonderful qualities.<br /><br />While I enjoyed Margaret as a character and took pleasure in witnessing her gradual transformation and personal growth, I couldn’t help but feel she was at times a little incongruent. On the one hand she is portrayed as a country girl – simple, refreshingly sincere – a doting sister, a daughter who greatly cherished everything about her father. But on the other hand, she also appears to be inconsiderate, self-centered, foolish, and haughty to others. Is she the “unaffected, spirited” beauty that Nathaniel fell in love with? Or is she a selfish and entitled heiress who can’t recall if she ever used the word “please” with a servant before?<br /><br />Despite my quibble about the heroine, this romantic tale by Julie Klassen was a terrific and exhilarating read that I could not easily put down! Looking for something that combines your love of Jane Austen and Downton Abbey? You should definitely try The Maid at Fairbourne Hall!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8430006500743202763" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/254819465?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kav" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kav" href="/user/show/6025638-kav">Kav</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer254819465" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8697084545709440657">I honestly don't know how Julie Klassen does it time and time again, but I am so grateful that she does. The Maid of Fairbourne Hall is just as stunning as her previous books. Stellar in fact. Brilliant. The kind of novel you want to escape into and never leave. Seriously, I read this in one sitting and it's 410 pages.! It wasn't that I couldn't put it down, it was that I refused to! What a perfect way to herald in the New Year! <br/><br/>First and foremost, her research is impeccable and she takes her re</span>
  <span id="freeText8697084545709440657" style="display:none">I honestly don't know how Julie Klassen does it time and time again, but I am so grateful that she does. The Maid of Fairbourne Hall is just as stunning as her previous books. Stellar in fact. Brilliant. The kind of novel you want to escape into and never leave. Seriously, I read this in one sitting and it's 410 pages.! It wasn't that I couldn't put it down, it was that I refused to! What a perfect way to herald in the New Year! <br /><br />First and foremost, her research is impeccable and she takes her readers into the belowstairs world of Regency England. That alone was fascinating -- but that we saw it all through the eyes of the aristocracy (Margaret) made so much more of an impact. And what a clever way to throw the heroine way out of her element! Definitely made for a page-turning read. <br /><br />And Margaret really comes into her own as the story progresses. She transforms from a self-centered young lady of means to a compassionate woman who learns to look beyond her own needs. A very satisfying personal journey. <br /><br />Add in the suspense over the threat of discovery and the romantic angle (which I can't say much about so as not to give anything away) and you will find The Maid of Fairbourne Hall an incredible and extremely satisfying read. Just clear your calendar before you pick it up because once you start reading, you won't want to stop! <br /><br />"Book has been provided courtesy of Baker Publishing Group and Graf-Martin Communications, Inc. Available at your favourite bookseller from Bethany House, a division of Baker Publishing Group."</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/268427910?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle Griep" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle Griep" href="/user/show/1872642-michelle-griep">Michelle Griep</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer268427910" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14105039327147948947">Author Julie Klassen’s writing gets better and better with each novel she pens. Translation: THE MAID OF FAIRBOURNE HALL is my absolute favorite of all her books. Why? Great question. Here’s a little dissection…<br/><br/>Tension<br/>Will the dashing Mr. Upchurch figure out that the love of his life is the one changing his chamber pot—or won’t he? I love that edge-of-the-seat kind of wondering, and this book delivers a fair amount of it.<br/><br/>Dilemma<br/>Heroine Margaret Macy is certainly in a pickle, and that’s what keep</span>
  <span id="freeText14105039327147948947" style="display:none">Author Julie Klassen’s writing gets better and better with each novel she pens. Translation: THE MAID OF FAIRBOURNE HALL is my absolute favorite of all her books. Why? Great question. Here’s a little dissection…<br /><br />Tension<br />Will the dashing Mr. Upchurch figure out that the love of his life is the one changing his chamber pot—or won’t he? I love that edge-of-the-seat kind of wondering, and this book delivers a fair amount of it.<br /><br />Dilemma<br />Heroine Margaret Macy is certainly in a pickle, and that’s what keeps a reader turning the pages. The outcome of her situation is cloaked until the very end.<br /><br />Characters to Admire<br />Hero Nathaniel Upchurch is such an upright and respectable man. Sure he’s got his faults, but underneath he’s a bulwark of what’s good and right in a human.<br /><br />Informational<br />One of the best things about Klassen’s books is that they’re full of fun facts about the Regency era. I always learn something about the period.<br /><br />Description<br />Who wouldn’t want to live in a manor house? And I did…leastwise for the few days it took me to read the story. I felt like I was there.<br /><br />THE MAID OF FAIRBOURNE HALL is a fantastic read full of romance, intrigue and a good reminder that it’s in our best interest to not judge others by merely outward appearance.<br /><br /><br /></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bluerose&#39;s  Heart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bluerose&#39;s  Heart" href="/user/show/3723392-bluerose-s-heart">Bluerose&#39;s  Heart</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3723392-bluerose-s-heart?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3723392-bluerose-s-heart?shelf=christian">christian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3723392-bluerose-s-heart?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer267638095" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3869202144144865565">I've had a really good reading streak lately. I've read some GREAT books! I've been depending more on my blogging friends to recommend books before requesting them, and it's made my reading time SO much better. (Thanks y'all!!!)<br/><br/>I'd already read from several bloggers that this book reminded them of Jane Austen. So, while reading this book, I was in the "Jane Austen" mindset. I enjoyed this book so much that if it wasn't for the huge pile of books I need to read, it would have been a perfect oppor</span>
  <span id="freeText3869202144144865565" style="display:none">I've had a really good reading streak lately. I've read some GREAT books! I've been depending more on my blogging friends to recommend books before requesting them, and it's made my reading time SO much better. (Thanks y'all!!!)<br /><br />I'd already read from several bloggers that this book reminded them of Jane Austen. So, while reading this book, I was in the "Jane Austen" mindset. I enjoyed this book so much that if it wasn't for the huge pile of books I need to read, it would have been a perfect opportunity to give a Jane Austen book another try. Even though I haven't seen much of Downtown Abbey, I've seen enough to know that this book also reminded me of that series. If you like it, this would be a good book to try.<br /><br />Some of my favorite books are when a person learns what it's like to walk in someone's else shoes, especially when it means the poor experience the rich life or vice versa. In The Maid of Fairbourne Hall, Margaret has to flee from her home on an attempt to save her reputation and purity. With no money, she has to take the job of a maid, and change her name to Nora, in an attempt to protect her anonymity. This is far from the life she's used to living. As you can suspect, a sweet romance is added in the mix. I enjoyed every moment of reading The Maid of Fairbourne Hall, and I desperately wished I could have read it quicker than I was allowed! ;)<br /><br />*A huge thanks to Bethany House for sending me a review copy in exchange for my honest opinion! </span>

<div id="review_184082459" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/184082459" />
    <a title="Margaret Chind" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/226769-margaret-chind"><img alt="Margaret Chind" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470101584p2/226769.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/184082459?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Margaret Chind" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Margaret Chind" href="/user/show/226769-margaret-chind">Margaret Chind</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/12954935-the-maid-of-fairbourne-hall">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/226769-margaret-chind?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/226769-margaret-chind?shelf=bethany-house">bethany-house</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/226769-margaret-chind?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/226769-margaret-chind?shelf=christian-historical-fiction">christian-historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/226769-margaret-chind?shelf=1810-1820-england-regency">1810-1820-england-regency</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer184082459" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7480314628096260168">In the fall of 2008 I first discovered <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/928415.Julie_Klassen' title='Julie Klassen' rel='nofollow noopener'>Julie Klassen</a> in her debut novel <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2043100.Lady_of_Milkweed_Manor' title='Lady of Milkweed Manor by Julie Klassen' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lady of Milkweed Manor</a> and fell in love. Pretty much as a matter of fact many things I said about that novel still hold true again to this one. <br/><br/>Upon finishing this novel, I sigh in complete contentment. This is near one of the best novels I have ever had the opportunity to fall deep within the pages and stay for a while.<br/><br/>From beginning to end I had my opinions of how things should go, with the slight twists and turns I never </span>
  <span id="freeText7480314628096260168" style="display:none">In the fall of 2008 I first discovered <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/928415.Julie_Klassen" title="Julie Klassen" rel="nofollow noopener">Julie Klassen</a> in her debut novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2043100.Lady_of_Milkweed_Manor" title="Lady of Milkweed Manor by Julie Klassen" rel="nofollow noopener">Lady of Milkweed Manor</a> and fell in love. Pretty much as a matter of fact many things I said about that novel still hold true again to this one. <br /><br />Upon finishing this novel, I sigh in complete contentment. This is near one of the best novels I have ever had the opportunity to fall deep within the pages and stay for a while.<br /><br />From beginning to end I had my opinions of how things should go, with the slight twists and turns I never had a clue how the plot would be. Sometimes I could not read fast enough, as a matter of fact most of the time. I would not believe certain things were happening.<br /><br />This is a perfect novel in regency time and I can see a bit of Austen and Jane Erye. I can easily say that readers of such will enjoy this story. It is alike, but completely unique and what a tale it tells. <br /><br />Then in the winter of 2009 I discovered more fabulous reading in her next novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3870943.The_Apothecary_s_Daughter" title="The Apothecary's Daughter by Julie Klassen" rel="nofollow noopener">The Apothecary's Daughter</a>, another piece of incredible historical fiction. This was the one where I discovered how much I truly enjoyed her introductions to each chapter with a quote or phrase. She continues that on into this novel as well with the quotes being straight out of resource that provide great insight into the working lives of the regency period. <br /><br />After that in 2010/2011 I read and loved her next two novels, both <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8125737.The_Girl_in_the_Gatehouse" title="The Girl in the Gatehouse by Julie Klassen" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl in the Gatehouse</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6624391.The_Silent_Governess" title="The Silent Governess by Julie Klassen" rel="nofollow noopener">The Silent Governess</a> which is possibly my favorite. Each time I venture into a novel from Julie I find entertainment and a lesson. While I can relate these to various films and other novels I've enjoyed this one about the serving class brings to mind a new favorite for me from Downton Abbey. <br /><br />If you like Jane Eyre, Austen, Downton Abbey and similar, you couldn't possibly not like this book. You'll love it just as much as I do. As in the words of other novels, imagine pirates from the glory of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15860733.M_L__Tyndall" title="M.L. Tyndall" rel="nofollow noopener">M.L. Tyndall</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1644459.Kaye_Dacus" title="Kaye Dacus" rel="nofollow noopener">Kaye Dacus</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/153441.Kathleen_Y_Barbo" title="Kathleen Y'Barbo" rel="nofollow noopener">Kathleen Y'Barbo</a>. Add to that the essence of character personality from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/52609.Deeanne_Gist" title="Deeanne Gist" rel="nofollow noopener">Deeanne Gist</a> and you might get a general idea of if this read is on you'd enjoy. I know I did. <br /><br />*Thanks to Julie and Bethany House Publishers for providing a copy for review.*<br /><br />Originally posted: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://creativemadnessmama.com/blog/2012/01/04/the-maid-of-fairbourne-hall-by-julie-klassen-2/">http://creativemadnessmama.com/blog/2...</a></span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review184082459">

<span id="freeTextContainer5203176997018066618">I have collected all of Julie Klassen's books, and I have to say, that this is one of the best. This book swept me away to another time and place, and I was so sad when the book ended, because it meant I had to leave. I love Regency-era England, and the descriptions in her books make me feel like I am there. I really got acquainted with Maidstone and Fairbourne Hall and the characters. I like the fact that characters who are not main characters are still rounded and developed. Excellent book, ex</span>
  <span id="freeText5203176997018066618" style="display:none">I have collected all of Julie Klassen's books, and I have to say, that this is one of the best. This book swept me away to another time and place, and I was so sad when the book ended, because it meant I had to leave. I love Regency-era England, and the descriptions in her books make me feel like I am there. I really got acquainted with Maidstone and Fairbourne Hall and the characters. I like the fact that characters who are not main characters are still rounded and developed. Excellent book, excellent plot. I enjoy the fact that she doesn't focus on a singular topic and stay narrowly focused on it, but explores problems outside of Margaret Macy's central issue, like that of slavery, pirates, duels, etc... I do wish that the romance side had been explored a teensy bit more. </span>

<div id="review_257150025" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/257150025" />
    <a title="Clare Cannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3655732-clare-cannon"><img alt="Clare Cannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416809580p2/3655732.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/257150025?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clare Cannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clare Cannon" href="/user/show/3655732-clare-cannon">Clare Cannon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Young Adults (females)</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3655732-clare-cannon?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer257150025" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2044608453402468855"><a href='http://www.goodreadingguide.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380334437i/693717.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>One of Klassen's better novels, Fairbourne Hall is a sweet Regency Romance with a faintly Christian tone. A well-to-do (somewhat spoiled) young woman is forced to flee her home when her step-father threatens to stoop to sordid means to force her marriage to his ne'er-do-well nephew, in order to gain access to her inheritance. She seeks to survive by assuming the role of a maid below-stairs, in what she belatedly learns is the home of an old acquaintance.<br/><br/>As many reviewers have noted, the nove</span>
  <span id="freeText2044608453402468855" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.goodreadingguide.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380334437i/693717.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>One of Klassen's better novels, Fairbourne Hall is a sweet Regency Romance with a faintly Christian tone. A well-to-do (somewhat spoiled) young woman is forced to flee her home when her step-father threatens to stoop to sordid means to force her marriage to his ne'er-do-well nephew, in order to gain access to her inheritance. She seeks to survive by assuming the role of a maid below-stairs, in what she belatedly learns is the home of an old acquaintance.<br><br>As many reviewers have noted, the novel has a strong 'Downtown Abbey' resemblance in the detailed (and I presume fairly accurate) descriptions of the servants' activities in a grand estate. The change is understandably a shock for young Margaret Macy, but the seriousness of her situation leaves her no choice but to try to survive. I was impressed that Klassen did not ease her character's burden by artificially shortening it, leaving her to follow through with her decision and throw herself completely into the role. Neither did Klassen make it so difficult that she fail miserably. Through genuine effort, with some falling into realistic mistakes and facing their consequences, our heroine demonstrates a realistic yet admirable strength of character that enables her to pull through.<br><br>A large part of the romance in the novel is the comparison of two different 'types' of men. The charming, flirtatious one who attracts the attention of every female is set against his more dutiful and far less exciting younger brother. The comparison lasts the entire story, and we are left with no uncertain picture of them both. The first proves most interested in women when they are out of his reach, as when they are courted by or married to another, or ineligible as a match, and his actions and their consequences are shown in all their ugliness. The second gradually proves himself the gentleman in his attitude and actions towards people of all classes, as well as an honest worker and capable manager of his own and others' affairs.<br><br>In the romance there is a distinction between passion and love, yet the author does dwell on brief moments of attraction that may not be helpful for younger readers.<br><br>While the detail may seem convoluted for those uninterested in Regency Romance, it is a sweet, enjoyable read that is perhaps one of the more worthwhile of its type. <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.GoodReadingGuide.com">www.GoodReadingGuide.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2044608453402468855" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_266269168" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/266269168" />
    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/369732-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470274836p2/369732.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/266269168?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/369732-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/369732-michelle?shelf=christianfiction">christianfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/369732-michelle?shelf=blog-tour-book">blog-tour-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/369732-michelle?shelf=historicalfiction">historicalfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/369732-michelle?shelf=books-you-will-find-my-name-in">books-you-will-find-my-name-in</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/369732-michelle?shelf=big-book-2012">big-book-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer266269168" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14484551616827452055">So far I have enjoyed reading the majority of Julie Klassen's historical romances. This one was no exception. The concept intrigued me from the outset, and the way the author pulled me in kept me reading was well done. At first the heroine wasn't very likable, but the author changed that by putting Margaret in a very humbling situation. Then the hero wasn't very likable, but once I was inside his head that all changed as well. I've never read a book where I disliked both main characters right of</span>
  <span id="freeText14484551616827452055" style="display:none">So far I have enjoyed reading the majority of Julie Klassen's historical romances. This one was no exception. The concept intrigued me from the outset, and the way the author pulled me in kept me reading was well done. At first the heroine wasn't very likable, but the author changed that by putting Margaret in a very humbling situation. Then the hero wasn't very likable, but once I was inside his head that all changed as well. I've never read a book where I disliked both main characters right off the bat, but because of the hardships endured by both parties, I gave them a chance. I'm glad I did.<br /><br />This story was a fairly long one, but I didn't feel like any part of the novel was not necessary to the plot, or used as filler. The surprising thing was I ended up liking several additional characters that I was not fond of at the book's onset. I'm not quite sure how the author did that, but she must have sold me on their behavior. I'm thinking the fact that they acted like real people would act made their situations more believable to me. I liked how the ruse continued and how difficult it was for Margaret to keep it going. The scene where the hero reveals that he knew who she really was made me a bit breathless. I wish their had been more scenes like that in the book.<br /><br />All in all, this was a captivating read. I always find stories where the rich are humbled by being forced into lower class situations -- usually in order to protect themselves -- quite intriguing. Because there is a bit of mystery to the story, I don't want to spoil it for the reader by giving away details that will take away from their experience. However, I can say that I loved the twists and how the author set things up. I also appreciated the spiritual arc in the story, though subtle for the most part. I found myself rooting for the characters to find love in the end. This was a nice read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14484551616827452055" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/190509397?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy" href="/user/show/1075341-kathy">Kathy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1075341-kathy?shelf=lost-love">lost-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1075341-kathy?shelf=2012">2012</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer190509397" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6582900394510356806">This kind of reminded me of Jane Austen’s Persuasion, with a twist. There is a bit of a lost-love story going on, which I’m always a sucker for. Margaret flees her home one evening and finds employment in the home of a man who once proposed to her. She wears a disguise and becomes a housemaid. I liked the changes Margaret goes through during her story. She starts off a bit pampered and kind of self-centered, but as the story progresses and she starts to actual work her personality softens and sh</span>
  <span id="freeText6582900394510356806" style="display:none">This kind of reminded me of Jane Austen’s Persuasion, with a twist. There is a bit of a lost-love story going on, which I’m always a sucker for. Margaret flees her home one evening and finds employment in the home of a man who once proposed to her. She wears a disguise and becomes a housemaid. I liked the changes Margaret goes through during her story. She starts off a bit pampered and kind of self-centered, but as the story progresses and she starts to actual work her personality softens and she begins to see people for who they really are. I thought it was a fun twist to have her working at an old “boyfriends” house. I admit though, I was a little disappointed that there weren’t more interactions between the two. I think it was about halfway through the book before they finally crossed paths. I would have liked more interactions, but the ones we do get were great. Overall, I enjoyed the story. You get to see behind the scenes of what the servants lives were like back then. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6582900394510356806" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2591977133" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2591977133" />
    <a title="J.T. IV" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22425568-j-t-iv"><img alt="J.T. IV" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442896643p2/22425568.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2591977133?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.T. IV" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.T. IV" href="/user/show/22425568-j-t-iv">J.T. IV</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22425568-j-t-iv?shelf=regency">regency</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22425568-j-t-iv?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2591977133" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16174685312453415702">Wonderful job by Ms. Klassen as usual of weaving history, excitement, and a bit of mystery and romance together. Appearances can be quite deceiving, and that is certainly true for Miss Macy as she flees one home disguised as a servant in order to try and save her vast inheritance. Her trip is complicated though as she is hired as a servant in the home or men she has rejected and who she now gets to see are not what she thought at all. Perhaps not my favorite background story of Ms. Klassen’s but</span>
  <span id="freeText16174685312453415702" style="display:none">Wonderful job by Ms. Klassen as usual of weaving history, excitement, and a bit of mystery and romance together. Appearances can be quite deceiving, and that is certainly true for Miss Macy as she flees one home disguised as a servant in order to try and save her vast inheritance. Her trip is complicated though as she is hired as a servant in the home or men she has rejected and who she now gets to see are not what she thought at all. Perhaps not my favorite background story of Ms. Klassen’s but ignoring that, the rest of the book is great. You begin to feel like Miss Macy is growing up, and while the developed relationship between the full time servants and her can be strained at times, it is still believable. If you like Regency period books and you appreciate that what truly matters is not the size of the bank account or the job position held, but the internal character of a person, I would very much recommend The Maid of Fairbourne Hall. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16174685312453415702" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13737552033052044748" style="display:none">I love the amount of history I know I will get when reading a Klassen novel. I love the deep characters and the twisting plots. I think this is my favorite of all her novels. I loved Downton Abby and loved being pulled back into the world of servants and the upper-class. But this one had a great twist with the spoiled rich girl learning a great life lesson.I was disappointed at first that the love interests got little time together but by the end the tension that she had built threw out the novel was all worth the wait. It reminded me a little of Persuasion:} These are clean romance novels with little bits of Christianity in their lives but no preaching, just good people trying to make good decisions.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/611109664" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/611109664?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jamie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jamie" href="/user/show/8586696-jamie">Jamie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8586696-jamie?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8586696-jamie?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer611109664" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11648033082039243699">I blame my recent lack of adequate sleep and lack of focus at work on this book. Not only did it have me pushing it when it came to bedtime, the next day at work I kept thinking about lunch (aka reading time) and what was going to happen. I should have known this was going to happen, because that’s what happens when you read a Julie Klassen novel.<br/><br/>And it was definitely no different with The Maid of Fairbourne Hall.<br/><br/>And I’ve decided she’s the Jane Austen of today.<br/><br/>And no more starting a sentence wit</span>
  <span id="freeText11648033082039243699" style="display:none">I blame my recent lack of adequate sleep and lack of focus at work on this book. Not only did it have me pushing it when it came to bedtime, the next day at work I kept thinking about lunch (aka reading time) and what was going to happen. I should have known this was going to happen, because that’s what happens when you read a Julie Klassen novel.<br /><br />And it was definitely no different with The Maid of Fairbourne Hall.<br /><br />And I’ve decided she’s the Jane Austen of today.<br /><br />And no more starting a sentence with and.<br /><br />I especially loved this one because it felt like reading a Jane Austen novel and like the set of Downton Abbey.<br /><br />Pampered Margaret Macy flees London in disguise to escape pressure to marry a dishonorable man. With no money and nowhere else to go, she takes a position as a housemaid in the home of Nathaniel Upchurch, a suitor she once rejected in hopes of winning his dashing brother. Praying no one will recognize her, Margaret fumbles through the first real work of her life. If she can last until her next birthday, she will gain an inheritance from a spinster aunt--and sweet independence. But can she remain hidden as a servant even when prying eyes visit Fairbourne Hall?<br /><br />Observing both brothers as an "invisible" servant, Margaret learns she may have misjudged Nathaniel. Is it too late to rekindle his admiration? And when one of the family is nearly killed, Margaret alone discovers who was responsible. Should she come forward, even at the risk of her reputation and perhaps her life? And can she avoid an obvious trap meant to force her from hiding?<br /><br />On her journey from wellborn lady to servant to uncertain future, Margaret must learn to look past appearances and find the true meaning of "serve one another in love."<br /><br />I pretty much pictured the different characters as ones from Downton (even if some of their personalities are different) and it kinda made reading it even more awesome! Except none of the characters you love die. Take a hint Downton. Quit killing people. But there is plenty of mystery, suspense, family and of course love.<br /><br />So next time I have a project to work on, the last thing I’m going to do right before is start a Julie Klassen novel.<br /><br />booksandbeverages.org</span>
  <a data-text-id="11648033082039243699" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_242223234" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/242223234" />
    <a title="Casey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3194216-casey"><img alt="Casey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476065155p2/3194216.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/242223234?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Casey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Casey" href="/user/show/3194216-casey">Casey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer242223234" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1388661901706045130">Writing a good regency must be a great deal more complicated than it looks upon first appearance. But when done in the correct and proper manner, good regency shines like the silver by which “Nora” polished belowstairs in Fairbourne Hall.<br/>	<br/>For anyone who has read even just a little of this period of fiction, one would not expect a rich society girl to one day be attending a masquerade ball and the next scrubbing a chamber pot. But as crazy as that sounds, the plot of the story perfectly supports </span>
  <span id="freeText1388661901706045130" style="display:none">Writing a good regency must be a great deal more complicated than it looks upon first appearance. But when done in the correct and proper manner, good regency shines like the silver by which “Nora” polished belowstairs in Fairbourne Hall.<br />	<br />For anyone who has read even just a little of this period of fiction, one would not expect a rich society girl to one day be attending a masquerade ball and the next scrubbing a chamber pot. But as crazy as that sounds, the plot of the story perfectly supports Margaret becoming “Nora” in a lowly maid.<br />	<br />For nearly four hundred pages I waited for the moment to come when she would be found out. And while she had many close calls that had me hanging by a single thread, becoming the servant she needed to be changed her in more ways than I think she expected. <br />	<br />Romance of course is varied and slow, but such is normal for this genre. Nathanial’s struggles to plant his feet squarely beneath him both financially and emotionally do not stop from making him a perfectly honorable and likeable hero. <br />	<br />Many subplots travel through the story and all play seamlessly into the main plot of the story. From a near murder attempt to “Nora’s” fear of being discovered, the story is one I looked forward to returning to time and again. And the romance is well worth the wait.<br />	<br />A very right and proper regency indeed.<br />	<br />This review is my honest opinion. Thanks to the publishers through CFBA for my copy to review. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1388661901706045130" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_283666426" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/283666426" />
    <a title="Booknut" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6917862-booknut"><img alt="Booknut" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411194489p2/6917862.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/283666426?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Booknut" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Booknut" href="/user/show/6917862-booknut">Booknut</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6917862-booknut?shelf=can-t-get-enough-of">can-t-get-enough-of</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6917862-booknut?shelf=heartbreak-and-loss">heartbreak-and-loss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6917862-booknut?shelf=heartwarming">heartwarming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6917862-booknut?shelf=ballgowns-and-intrigue">ballgowns-and-intrigue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6917862-booknut?shelf=strong-and-kickass-heroines">strong-and-kickass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6917862-booknut?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6917862-booknut?shelf=books-i-love-dearly">books-i-love-dearly</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6917862-booknut?shelf=forever-re-read">forever-re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6917862-booknut?shelf=ethics-and-society">ethics-and-society</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6917862-booknut?shelf=knight-in-shining-armour">knight-in-shining-armour</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer283666426" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15745332153377760675">A tale of a headstrong young lady of high standing who - when her freedom, inheritance and personal safety is under attack in her own home by her ghastly stepfather and his nephew - flees London in the hopes of escaping her past and her fears, disguised as a maid. Due to unlikely circumstances, she finds herself accepting a position at Fairbourne Hall - the very place wherein live two brothers who have both played major roles in Margaret's past. Lewis, the sought-after rogue and Nate, the dark, </span>
  <span id="freeText15745332153377760675" style="display:none">A tale of a headstrong young lady of high standing who - when her freedom, inheritance and personal safety is under attack in her own home by her ghastly stepfather and his nephew - flees London in the hopes of escaping her past and her fears, disguised as a maid. Due to unlikely circumstances, she finds herself accepting a position at Fairbourne Hall - the very place wherein live two brothers who have both played major roles in Margaret's past. Lewis, the sought-after rogue and Nate, the dark, headstrong younger brother who's heart Margaret broke some time ago. Now she must keep up pretences, evade her stepfather, succeed at her new and lowly occupation as well as try very hard not to fall for one - or both - of the brothers yet again.<br /><br />But don't be fooled by appearances! Margaret is not your average lovestruck maiden - she is stubborn and intelligent, overcoming obstacles and acting with great tact and heart, in the sense that she feels for others and condones her own past actions and the person she was. Margaret - who takes on the name of 'Nora' - becomes a different person through her experiences, as she realises that not only should you not judge a book by its cover, but that it is possible to read a book again and find new meaning in it, or spot something you overlooked the first time. Not once does she let her feeling for either of the brothers interfere with her duties, her roles, or her relationships with others - instead, she manages to find a balance and in finding that balance, she begins to understand herself with new eyes. This is especially evident, I think, in the second last scene when she confronts her stepfather. She is still Margaret - but she is the Margaret that she had always tried to push away, to silence; the kind of girl who isn't afraid to stand up for what is right and to exert her authority in order to see justice done.<br /><br />Perfectly written, with enthralling sprinkles of my favourite kind of Austen-y writing and jovial lines, this book is definitely up to scratch with Klassen's classic writing. I have read three of her novels and it is impossible to decide on a favourite. Her characters become your friends; these wilful, intelligent and courageous young heroines who find their own happy endings by laying their own paths down and fighting for it every inch of the way.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15745332153377760675" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
